1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Cross-Org gRPC Service Definition Discovery

## Your Task

Find the gRPC service definitions that are shared between `envoyproxy/envoy` and `grpc/grpc`. Specifically: 1. In `envoyproxy/data-plane-api`, find all `.proto` files that define `service` declarations using `rpc` methods (the xDS service definitions). 2. In `grpc/grpc`, find the source files that implement the `grpc_health_v1.Health` service (the standard gRPC health checking protocol). Report the repo, file path, and service name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Excellent! I've successfully created a comprehensive analysis of gRPC service definitions shared between the repositories. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I've discovered gRPC service definitions across **envoyproxy/data-plane-api** and **grpc/grpc**:

### Data-Plane-API Services (27 files)
**Core xDS (Extensible Discovery Service) APIs:**
- **AggregatedDiscoveryService** - multiplexes multiple resource types (v2 and v3)
- **ClusterDiscoveryService** - manages cluster definitions
- **EndpointDiscoveryService** - manages endpoint configurations
- **ListenerDiscoveryService** - manages listener configurations
- **RouteDiscoveryService** & **VirtualHostDiscoveryService** - manage routing
- **ScopedRoutesDiscoveryService** - manages scoped routing
- **SecretDiscoveryService** - manages secrets (v2 and v3)
- **RuntimeDiscoveryService** - manages runtime configurations (v2 and v3)
- **LocalityEndpointDiscoveryService** - manages locality-specific endpoints

**Additional Services:**
- **HealthDiscoveryService** - Envoy health checking
- **AccessLogService** - streaming access logs
- **MetricsService** - streaming metrics
- **Authorization** service - external authorization
- **ExternalProcessor** - external request/response processing
- **LoadReportingService** - load statistics reporting
- **RateLimitService** - rate limiting
- **TapSinkService** - tap sink for request capture

### gRPC Health Service (2 files)
- **Health service** - standard gRPC health checking protocol with `Check` (unary) and `Watch` (streaming) RPC methods
  - Located in: `src/proto/grpc/health/v1/health.proto` and `src/python/grpcio_health_checking/grpc_health/v1/health.proto`

The complete analysis has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed file paths and service names.

Consider\\n131:   //   this example sequence of updates:\\n132:   //\\n133:   //   * Management server applies a canary config successfully.\\n134:   //   * Management server rolls back to a production config.\\n135:   //   * Envoy rejects the new production config.\\n136:   //\\n137:   //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\\n138:   //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\\n139:   //   clean slate.\\n140:   //\\n141:   // * ``--dry-run-canary``. When set, a canary response will never be applied, only\\n142:   //   validated via a dry run.\\n143:   //\\n144:   bool canary = 3;\\n145: \\n146:   // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\\n147:   // Must be consistent with the ``type_url`` in the 'resources' repeated Any (if non-empty).\\n148:   string type_url = 4;\\n149: \\n150:   // For gRPC based subscriptions, the nonce provides a way to explicitly ack a\\n151:   // specific ``DiscoveryResponse`` in a following ``DiscoveryRequest``. Additional\\n152:   // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\\n153:   // previous version on the stream prior to this ``DiscoveryResponse``, that were\\n154:   // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\\n155:   // to ignore any further ``DiscoveryRequests`` for the previous version until a\\n156:   // ``DiscoveryRequest`` bearing the nonce. The nonce is optional and is not\\n157:   // required for non-stream based xDS implementations.\\n158:   string nonce = 5;\\n159: \\n160:   // The control plane instance that sent the response.\\n161:   config.core.v3.ControlPlane control_plane = 6;\\n162: \\n163:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n164:   // Errors associated with specific resources. Clients are expected to\\n165:   // remember the most recent error for a given resource across responses;\\n166:   // the error condition is not considered to be cleared until a response is\\n167:   // received that contains the resource in the 'resources' field.\\n168:   repeated ResourceError resource_errors = 7;\\n169: }\\n170: \\n171: // DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\\n172: // endpoint for Delta xDS.\\n173: //\\n174: // With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\\n175: // snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\\n176: // diff to the state of a xDS client.\\n177: // In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\\n178: // the resource granularity.\\n179: // An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\\n180: // stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\\n181: // connected to it.\\n182: //\\n183: // In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\\n184: // ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\\n185: // Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\\n186: // debugging purposes only.\\n187: //\\n188: // ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\\n189: // can be either or both of:\\n190: //\\n191: // * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\\n192: //   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\\n193: // * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\\n194: //   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\\n195: //\\n196: // Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\\n197: // has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\\n198: // that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\\n199: //\\n200: // As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\\n201: // all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\\n202: // a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\\n203: // In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \\\"start\\\" of every\\n204: // gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\\n205: // ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n206: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n207: message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\\n208:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\\\";\\n209: \\n210:   // The node making the request.\\n211:   config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\\n212: \\n213:   // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\\n214:   // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This does not need to be set if\\n215:   // resources are only referenced via ``xds_resource_subscribe`` and\\n216:   // ``xds_resources_unsubscribe``.\\n217:   string type_url = 2;\\n218: \\n219:   // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\\n220:   // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\\n221:   // All resource names in the ``resource_names_subscribe`` list are added to the\\n222:   // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the ``resource_names_unsubscribe``\\n223:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\\n224:   //\\n225:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty ``resource_names_subscribe`` or\\n226:   // ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` list simply means that no resources are to be\\n227:   // added or removed to the resource list.\\n228:   // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\\n229:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\\n230:   //\\n231:   // .. note::\\n232:   //   The server must respond with all resources listed in ``resource_names_subscribe``,\\n233:   //   even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\\n234:   //   the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\\n235:   //   to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\\n236:   //\\n237:   // These two fields can be set in any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``, including ACKs\\n238:   // and ``initial_resource_versions``.\\n239:   //\\n240:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\\n241:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\\n242: \\n243:   // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\\n244:   repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\\n245: \\n246:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n247:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_subscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n248:   // along with each resource name.\\n249:   //\\n250:   // .. note::\\n251:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n252:   //   in ``resource_names_subscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_subscribe``.\\n253:   //\\n254:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_subscribe = 8;\\n255: \\n256:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\\n257:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\\n258:   // along with each resource name.\\n259:   //\\n260:   // .. note::\\n261:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\\n262:   //   in ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_unsubscribe``.\\n263:   //\\n264:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\\n265: \\n266:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\\n267:   // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\\n268:   // It will not be populated:\\n269:   //\\n270:   // * In the very first stream of a session, since the client will not yet have any resources.\\n271:   // * In any message after the first in a stream (for a given ``type_url``), since the server will\\n272:   //   already be correctly tracking the client's state.\\n273:   //\\n274:   // (In ADS, the first message ``of each type_url`` of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\\n275:   // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the xDS client.\\n276:   // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\\n277:   map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\\n278: \\n279:   // When the ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` is a ACK or NACK message in response\\n280:   // to a previous ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``, the ``response_nonce`` must be the\\n281:   // nonce in the ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``.\\n282:   // Otherwise (unlike in ``DiscoveryRequest``) ``response_nonce`` must be omitted.\\n283:   string response_nonce = 6;\\n284: \\n285:   // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryResponse>`\\n286:   // failed to update configuration. The ``message`` field in ``error_details``\\n287:   // provides the Envoy internal exception related to the failure.\\n288:   google.rpc.Status error_detail = 7;\\n289: }\\n290: \\n291: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n292: message DeltaDiscoveryResponse {\\n293:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type =\\n294:       \\\"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryResponse\\\";\\n295: \\n296:   // The version of the response data (used for debugging).\\n297:   string system_version_info = 1;\\n298: \\n299:   // The response resources. These are typed resources, whose types must match\\n300:   // the ``type_url`` field.\\n301:   repeated Resource resources = 2;\\n302: \\n303:   // field id 3 IS available!\\n304: \\n305:   // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\\n306:   // Must be consistent with the ``type_url`` in the Any within 'resources' if 'resources' is non-empty.\\n307:   string type_url = 4;\\n308: \\n309:   // Resource names of resources that have been deleted and to be removed from the xDS Client.\\n310:   // Removed resources for missing resources can be ignored.\\n311:   repeated string removed_resources = 6;\\n312: \\n313:   // Alternative to ``removed_resources`` that allows specifying which variant of\\n314:   // a resource is being removed. This variant must be used for any resource\\n315:   // for which dynamic parameter constraints were sent to the client.\\n316:   repeated ResourceName removed_resource_names = 8;\\n317: \\n318:   // The nonce provides a way for ``DeltaDiscoveryRequests`` to uniquely\\n319:   // reference a ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` when (N)ACKing. {\\n343:   // A single constraint for a given key.\\n344:   message SingleConstraint {\\n345:     message Exists {\\n346:     }\\n347: \\n348:     // The key to match against.\\n349:     string key = 1;\\n350: \\n351:     oneof constraint_type {\\n352:       option (validate.required) = true;\\n353: \\n354:       // Matches this exact value.\\n355:       string value = 2;\\n356: \\n357:       // Key is present (matches any value except for the key being absent).\\n358:       // This allows setting a default constraint for clients that do\\n359:       // not send a key at all, while there may be other clients that need\\n360:       // special configuration based on that key.\\n361:       Exists exists = 3;\\n362:     }\\n363:   }\\n364: \\n365:   message ConstraintList {\\n366:     // A list of constraints that match if any one constraint in the list\\n374:     // matches.\\n375:     ConstraintList or_constraints = 2;\\n376: \\n377:     // A list of constraints that must all match.\\n378:     ConstraintList and_constraints = 3;\\n379: \\n380:     // The inverse (NOT) of a set of constraints.\\n381:     DynamicParameterConstraints not_constraints = 4;\\n382:   }\\n383: }\\n384: \\n385: // [#next-free-field: 10]\\n386: message Resource {\\n387:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \\\"envoy.api.v2.Resource\\\";\\n388: \\n389:   // Cache This does not need to be set if\n215:   // resources are only referenced via ``xds_resource_subscribe`` and\n216:   // ``xds_resources_unsubscribe``.\n217:   string type_url = 2;\n218: \n219:   // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\n220:   // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\n221:   // All resource names in the ``resource_names_subscribe`` list are added to the\n222:   // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the ``resource_names_unsubscribe``\n223:   // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\n224:   //\n225:   // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty ``resource_names_subscribe`` or\n226:   // ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` list simply means that no resources are to be\n227:   // added or removed to the resource list.\n228:   // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\n229:   // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\n230:   //\n231:   // .. note::\n232:   //   The server must respond with all resources listed in ``resource_names_subscribe``,\n233:   //   even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\n234:   //   the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\n235:   //   to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\n236:   //\n237:   // These two fields can be set in any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``, including ACKs\n238:   // and ``initial_resource_versions``.\n239:   //\n240:   // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\n241:   repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\n242: \n243:   // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\n244:   repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\n245: \n246:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n247:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_subscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\n248:   // along with each resource name.\n249:   //\n250:   // .. note::\n251:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\n252:   //   in ``resource_names_subscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_subscribe``.\n253:   //\n254:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_subscribe = 8;\n255: \n256:   // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n257:   // Alternative to ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\n258:   // along with each resource name.\n259:   //\n260:   // .. note::\n261:   //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\n262:   //   in ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_unsubscribe``.\n263:   //\n264:   repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\n265: \n266:   // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\n267:   // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\n268:   // It will not be populated:\n269:   //\n270:   // * In the very first stream of a session, since the client will not yet have any resources.\n271:   // * In any message after the first in a stream (for a given ``type_url``), since the server will\n272:   //   already be correctly tracking the client's state.\n273:   //\n274:   // (In ADS, the first message ``of each type_url`` of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\n275:   // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the xDS client.\n276:   // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\n277:   map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\n278: \n279:   // When the ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` is a ACK or NACK message in response\n280:   // to a previous ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``, the ``response_nonce`` must be the\n281:   // nonce in the ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``.\n282:   // Otherwise (unlike in ``DiscoveryRequest``) ``response_nonce`` must be omitted.\n283:   string response_nonce = 6;\n284: \n285:   // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryResponse>`\n286:   // failed to update configuration. The ``message`` field in ``error_details``\n287:   // provides the Envoy internal exception related to the failure.\n288:   google.rpc.Status error_detail = 7;\n289: }\n290: \n291: // [#next-free-field: 10]\n292: message DeltaDiscoveryResponse {\n293:   option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type =\n294:       \"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryResponse\";\n295: \n296:   // The version of the response data (used for debugging).\n297:   string system_version_info = 1;\n298: \n299:   // The response resources.     "content": "1: syntax = \"proto3\";\n2: \n3: package envoy.service.ext_proc.v3;\n4: \n5: import \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\n6: import \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\n7: import \"envoy/type/v3/http_status.proto\";\n8: \n9: import \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\n10: import \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n11: \n12: import \"xds/annotations/v3/status.proto\";\n13: \n14: import \"envoy/annotations/deprecation.proto\";\n15: import \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\n16: import \"validate/validate.proto\";\n17: \n18: option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.service.ext_proc.v3\";\n19: option java_outer_classname = \"ExternalProcessorProto\";\n20: option java_multiple_files = true;\n21: option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/service/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n22: option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n23: \n24: // [#protodoc-title: External processing service]\n25: \n26: // A service that can access and modify HTTP requests and responses as part of a filter chain.\n27: // The overall external processing protocol works like this:\n28: //\n29: // 1. The data plane sends to the service information about the HTTP request.\n30: // 2. The service sends back a ``ProcessingResponse`` message that directs the data plane to either\n31: //    stop processing, continue without it, or send it the next chunk of the message body.\n32: // 3. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the message body in chunks, or the entire\n33: //    body at once. In either case, the server may send back a ``ProcessingResponse`` for each\n34: //    message it receives, or wait for a certain amount of body chunks to be received before\n35: //    streaming back the ``ProcessingResponse`` messages.\n36: // 4. If so requested, the data plane sends the server the HTTP trailers, and the server sends back\n37: //    a ``ProcessingResponse``.\n38: // 5. At this point, request processing is done, and we pick up again at step 1 when the data plane\n39: //    receives a response from the upstream server.\n40: // 6. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream cleanly, then the data plane\n41: //    proceeds without consulting the server.\n42: // 7. At any point above, if the server closes the gRPC stream with an error, then the data plane\n43: //    returns a ``500`` error to the client, unless the filter was configured to ignore errors.\n44: //\n45: // In other words, the process is a request/response conversation, but using a gRPC stream to make\n46: // it easier for the server to maintain state.\n47: service ExternalProcessor {\n48:   // This begins the bidirectional stream that the data plane will use to\n49:   // give the server control over what the filter does.
